By early 1985, the Macintosh's failure to defeat the IBM PC[\[124\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2015185%E2%80%93187-124)[\[125\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlender201684%E2%80%9388-125) triggered a power struggle between Jobs and CEO [John Sculley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Sculley "John Sculley"), who had been hired two years earlier by Jobs[\[132\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-FOOTNOTELinzmayer2004156-132)[\[133\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2015153%E2%80%93154-133) using the famous line, "Do you want to sell sugar water for the rest of your life or come with me and change the world?"[\[134\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-134) Sculley and Jobs' visions for the company greatly differed. The former favored [open architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_architecture "Open architecture") computers like the Apple II, sold to education, small business, and home markets less vulnerable to IBM. Jobs wanted the company to focus on the [closed architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Closed_architecture "Closed architecture") Macintosh as a business alternative to the IBM PC. President and CEO Sculley had little control over chairman of the Board Jobs' Macintosh division; it and the Apple II division operated like separate companies, duplicating services.[\[135\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-robbeloth198510_11-135) Although its products provided 85% of Apple's sales in early 1985, the company's January 1985 [annual meeting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annual_meeting "Annual meeting") did not mention the Apple II division or employees. This frustrated Wozniak, who left active employment at Apple in the spring of that year to pursue other ventures, stating that the company had "been going in the wrong direction for the last five years" and sold most of his stock.[\[136\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-rice19850415-136)[\[137\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-wozemployee-137)[\[138\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-138) Despite these grievances, Wozniak left the company amicably and as of January2018[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Apple_Inc.&action=edit) continued to represent Apple at events or in interviews,[\[137\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-wozemployee-137) receiving a stipend over the years for this role estimated in 2006 to be $120,000 per year.[\[139\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-iWoz-139) Wozniak also remained an Apple shareholder following his departure.[\[140\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-wozstock-140)

Wozniak's first venture after leaving Apple was founding [CL 9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CL_9 "CL 9") in 1985 and creating the first programmable [universal remote](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_remote "Universal remote") control two years later, called the "CORE", stating that "I never felt like I was turning my back on my own company \[Apple\]." He told Apple's director of engineering [Wayne Rosing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Rosing "Wayne Rosing") about his decision to step away from the company, but not his longtime business partner and friend Steve Jobs. Wozniak guessed that Jobs first heard the news from an article in _[The Wall Street Journal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal "The Wall Street Journal")_ where he mentioned that he wasn't leaving because he was disgruntled with Apple, but that he was excited to build a new remote control. The article nevertheless included some of Wozniak's criticisms of Apple, and Wozniak later said "it was an accident, but it's been picked up by every book and every bit of history \[since\]."[\[139\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-iWoz-139):289

In April 1985, Sculley decided to remove Jobs as the general manager of the Macintosh division, and gained unanimous support from the Apple board of directors.[\[141\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlender201687%E2%80%9392-141)[\[132\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-FOOTNOTELinzmayer2004156-132) Rather than submit to Sculley's direction, Jobs attempted to oust him from his leadership role at Apple.[\[142\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-FOOTNOTELinzmayer2004156%E2%80%93157-142) Informed by [Jean-Louis Gassée](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Louis_Gass%C3%A9e "Jean-Louis Gassée"), Sculley found out that Jobs had been attempting to organize a [coup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coup_d'%C3%A9tat#Other "Coup d'état") and called an emergency executive meeting at which Apple's executive staff sided with Sculley and stripped Jobs of all operational duties.[\[142\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-FOOTNOTELinzmayer2004156%E2%80%93157-142)

Jobs, while taking the position of chairman of the firm, had no influence over Apple's direction and resigned in September 1985, taking a number of Apple employees with him to found [NeXT Inc.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NeXT "NeXT")[\[143\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-143) In a show of defiance at being set aside by Apple Computer, Jobs sold all but one of his 6.5 million shares in the company for $70 million. Jobs then acquired the [visual effects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual_effects "Visual effects") house, [Pixar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pixar "Pixar") for $5M (equivalent to $14,700,000in 2025). NeXT Inc. built computers with futuristic designs and the UNIX-derived [NEXTSTEP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NEXTSTEP "NEXTSTEP") operating system. NeXTSTEP eventually developed into Mac OS X. While not a commercial success, due in part to its high price, the NeXT computer introduced important concepts to the history of the personal computer, including serving as the initial platform for [Tim Berners-Lee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee "Tim Berners-Lee") as he was developing the [World Wide Web](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web "World Wide Web").[\[144\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-144)

Sculley reorganized the company, unifying sales and marketing in one division and product operations and development in another.[\[145\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-145)[\[135\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-robbeloth198510_11-135) Despite initial marketing difficulties, the Macintosh brand was eventually a success for Apple, due to its introduction of [desktop publishing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desktop_publishing "Desktop publishing")[\[146\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-pournelle198712-146) (and later [computer animation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_animation "Computer animation")) through Apple's partnership with [Adobe Systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adobe_Systems "Adobe Systems"). This partnership bore both the [LaserWriter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LaserWriter "LaserWriter") printer, one of the first commercially successful laser printers (containing a built-in interpreter for Adobe's [PostScript](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PostScript "PostScript") page description language), and [Aldus PageMaker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aldus_PageMaker "Aldus PageMaker"), the first commercially successful desktop publishing software. The Macintosh became the default platform for many arts industries including cinema, music, advertising, and publishing.

## 1985–1997: Sculley, Spindler, Amelio

> Apple is a lot like Italy. It's a highly creative company, but with that comes chaos.

— [Regis McKenna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regis_McKenna "Regis McKenna")[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-fortune19960219-147)

### Corporate performance

See also: [List of mergers and acquisitions by Apple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_mergers_and_acquisitions_by_Apple "List of mergers and acquisitions by Apple")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Macintosh_SE.jpg/500px-Macintosh_SE.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Macintosh_SE.jpg) [Macintosh SE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh_SE "Macintosh SE") (1987)

Under leadership of [John Sculley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Sculley "John Sculley"), Apple issued its first corporate stock dividend on May 11, 1987. A month later on June 16, Apple stock split for the first time in a 2:1 split. Between March 1988 and January 1989, Apple undertook five acquisitions, including software companies Network Innovations,[\[148\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-148) Styleware,[\[149\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-149) Nashoba Systems,[\[150\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-150) and Coral Software,[\[151\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-151) as well as satellite communications company Orion Network Systems.[\[152\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-152)

Apple continued to sell both lines of its computers, the Apple II and the Macintosh. A few months after introducing the Mac, Apple released a compact version of the Apple II called the [Apple IIc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_IIc "Apple IIc"). And in 1986 Apple introduced the [Apple IIGS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_IIGS "Apple IIGS"), an Apple II positioned as something of a hybrid product with a mouse-driven, Mac-like operating environment. Even with the release of the first Macintosh, Apple II computers remained the main source of income for Apple for years.[\[153\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-153)

### The Mac family

See also: [Timeline of Macintosh models](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_Macintosh_models "Timeline of Macintosh models")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Powerbook_100_pose.jpg/500px-Powerbook_100_pose.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Powerbook_100_pose.jpg) [PowerBook 100](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PowerBook_100 "PowerBook 100") (1991)

At the same time, the Mac was becoming a product family of its own. The original model evolved into the [Mac Plus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh_Plus "Macintosh Plus") in 1986 and spawned the [Mac SE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh_SE "Macintosh SE") and the [Mac II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh_II "Macintosh II") in 1987 and the [Mac Classic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh_Classic "Macintosh Classic") and [Mac LC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh_LC "Macintosh LC") in 1990. Meanwhile, Apple attempted its first portable Macs: the failed [Macintosh Portable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh_Portable "Macintosh Portable") in 1989 and then the more popular [PowerBook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PowerBook "PowerBook") in 1991, a landmark product that established the modern form and [ergonomic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ergonomics "Ergonomics") layout of the laptop. Popular products and increasing revenues made this a good time for Apple. [MacAddict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacAddict "MacAddict") magazine has called 1989 to 1991 the "first golden age" of the Macintosh.

### Early-mid-1990s

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Apple_Newton_MessagePad_100_with_stylus.jpg/500px-Apple_Newton_MessagePad_100_with_stylus.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Apple_Newton_MessagePad_100_with_stylus.jpg) [Apple Newton MessagePad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MessagePad "MessagePad") (1993)

In the late 1980s, Apple's fiercest technological rivals were the [Amiga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amiga "Amiga") and [Atari ST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atari_ST "Atari ST") platforms. But computers based on the [IBM PC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM_PC "IBM PC") were far more popular than all three, and by the 1990s, they finally had a comparable [GUI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GUI "GUI") thanks to [Windows 3.0](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_3.0 "Windows 3.0"), and were out-competing Apple.

Apple's response to the PC threat was a profusion of new Macintosh lines including [Quadra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh_Quadra "Macintosh Quadra"), [Centris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh_Centris "Macintosh Centris"), and [Performa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macintosh_Performa "Macintosh Performa"). These new lines were marketed poorly by what was now "arguably one of the worst-managed companies in the industry". There were too many models, differentiated by very minor graduations in [technical specifications](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technical_specifications "Technical specifications"). The profusion of arbitrary model numbers confused consumers and hurt Apple's reputation for simplicity. Resellers like [Sears](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sears,_Roebuck_and_Company "Sears, Roebuck and Company") and [CompUSA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CompUSA "CompUSA") often failed to sell or even competently display these Macs. Inventory grew as Apple consistently underestimated demand for popular models and overestimated demand for others.[\[154\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-alsop19960205-154)

In 1991, Apple partnered with long-time competitor [IBM](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM "IBM") and [Motorola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motorola "Motorola") to form the [AIM alliance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AIM_alliance "AIM alliance"), with the ultimate goal to create a revolutionary new computing platform, known as [PReP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PReP "PReP"), using IBM and Motorola hardware and Apple software. As the first step, Apple started the [Power Macintosh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_Macintosh "Power Macintosh") line in 1994, using [PowerPC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PowerPC "PowerPC") processors from Motorola and IBM. The [RISC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RISC "RISC") architecture of these processors differed substantially from the [Motorola 68000 series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motorola_68000_series "Motorola 68000 series") architecture used by previous Macs. Parts of Apple's operating system were rewritten to allow some older Mac software to run in [emulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emulator "Emulator") on the PowerPC series.\[ _[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_\] In 1993, Apple released the [Newton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newton_(platform) "Newton (platform)"), an early [personal digital assistant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personal_digital_assistant "Personal digital assistant") (PDA).

Apple by the mid-1990s was nonetheless in such serious difficulty that CFO Jim Graziano in 1995 asked the board of directors to find a buyer because the company was no longer financially viable, and quit when the board refused.[\[155\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-seymour19960109-155) _Fortune_ in February 1996 wrote "the company that invented the personal computer will likely disappear". Noting that by the time readers received the magazine the company might be acquired by [Sun Microsystems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun_Microsystems "Sun Microsystems") or [Philips Electronics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philips_Electronics "Philips Electronics"), _Fortune_ said that $1,000 invested in Apple stock ten years earlier would be worth $2,900, compared to $22,000 in [Compaq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compaq "Compaq").[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-fortune19960219-147)

Contributing to Apple's problems was its inability to manufacture enough PowerPC-based Macintoshes to meet demand.[\[155\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-seymour19960109-155) Aware of the company's lack of scale, Apple had by then repeatedly sought larger partners for a decade. It almost persuaded [Digital Equipment Corporation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_Equipment_Corporation "Digital Equipment Corporation") (DEC) to have the former manage the latter's personal computer business;[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-fortune19960219-147) it refused IBM's offer to purchase the company, but later unsuccessfully sought another IBM offer;[\[156\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-markoff19970901-156) and at one point was "hours away" from an acquisition by Sun,[\[154\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-alsop19960205-154)[\[157\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-preimesberger20110225-157) one of several attempts by Sun to buy the company. Markkula said during Sun merger negotiations, "Since 1986, we held serious discussions with DEC, [Kodak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kodak "Kodak"), [Sony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sony "Sony"), Sun, Compaq, IBM, and other companies I'd rather not name now. They were very thoughtful discussions. We considered everything from 'Let's trade technology' to 'Let's put the companies together' with each one of them".[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-fortune19960219-147)

### Need for a new OS

In 1994 Apple launched [eWorld](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EWorld "EWorld"), an online service providing email, news and a bulletin board system to replace [AppleLink](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AppleLink "AppleLink"). It was shut down in 1996.[\[158\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-158) In 1995, to achieve deeper market penetration and extra revenue, Apple officially began licensing the Mac OS and Macintosh ROMs to 3rd party manufacturers. The " [Clonintoshes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clonintosh "Clonintosh")" competed with Apple's own Mac's and reduced Apple's sales.[\[159\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-lemjosh-159) Apple had market share of over 10% until Jobs was re-hired in 1997 as interim CEO to replace Gil Amelio, and found a loophole to terminate the Macintosh OS licensing program. Macintosh's market share fell to around 3%.[\[160\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-160)

Among Apple's most important needs was a new operating system.[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-fortune19960219-147) During the 90's, "project _Pink_" had Apple and IBM collaborating to develop a new operating system, named _[Taligent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taligent "Taligent")_ to replace _[System 7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_7 "System 7")_. Infighting resulted in Apple leaving the project and IBM finishing it. Apple started project _[Copland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copland_(operating_system) "Copland (operating system)")_, another effort to replace System 7, but it was affected by [Feature creep](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feature_creep "Feature creep") then [Development hell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Development_hell "Development hell") due to software planned for Taligent being reworked for Copland. Ultimately Copland was scrapped.[\[161\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-161) With the Copland project in disarray, Apple decided it needed to acquire another company's operating system. Candidates considered were [Sun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun_Microsystems "Sun Microsystems")'s [Solaris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solaris_(operating_system) "Solaris (operating system)") and [Windows NT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_NT "Windows NT"). Hancock was in favor of Solaris, while Amelio preferred Windows. Amelio called [Bill Gates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Gates "Bill Gates"), and Gates promised Microsoft engineers would port [QuickDraw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/QuickDraw "QuickDraw") to NT.[\[162\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-162)

### Acquisition of NeXT

In 1996, the struggling [NeXT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NeXT "NeXT") company beat Be Inc.'s [BeOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BeOS "BeOS") bid to sell its operating system to Apple.[\[163\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-163) On December 20, 1996, Apple announced it would purchase NeXT, and its NeXTstep operating system, for $429 million and 1.5 million shares of Apple stock.[\[164\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-apple-acquisition-164) This brought Jobs back to Apple's management for the first time since 1985, and NeXT technology became the foundation of the [Mac OS X](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mac_OS_X "Mac OS X") operating system.

## 1997–2001: Apple's comeback

> If I were running Apple, I would milk the Macintosh for all it's worth--and get busy on the next great thing. The PC wars are over. Done. Microsoft won a long time ago.

—Jobs, February 1996[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-fortune19960219-147)

### Return of Steve Jobs

On July 9, 1997, [Gil Amelio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gil_Amelio "Gil Amelio") was ousted as CEO of Apple by the board of directors. [Fred D. Anderson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fred_D._Anderson "Fred D. Anderson") was the head of the directors in short term and obtained short-term working capital from the banks in July 1997.[\[165\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-165)[\[166\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-166) In August 1997, Jobs stepped in as the interim CEO to begin a critical restructuring of the company's product line.[\[5\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-interim_CEO-5) He eventually became CEO and served in that position from January 2000 to August 2011.[\[6\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-norr-6) On August 24, 2011, Jobs resigned his position as chief executive officer of Apple before his long battle with pancreatic cancer took his life on October 5, 2011.[\[167\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-167) On November 10, 1997, Apple introduced the [Apple Store](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Store_(online) "Apple Store (online)"), an online retail store based upon the [WebObjects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WebObjects "WebObjects") application server the company had acquired in its purchase of [NeXT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NeXT "NeXT"). The new direct sales outlet was tied to a new build-to-order manufacturing strategy.[\[168\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-168)[\[169\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-169)

### Microsoft deal

At the 1997 [Macworld Expo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macworld_Expo "Macworld Expo"), Jobs announced that Apple would begin a partnership with [Microsoft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft "Microsoft"), with terms including a five-year commitment from Microsoft to release [Microsoft Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Office "Microsoft Office") for Macintosh, and a US$150 million investment in Apple. The long-standing dispute over whether Windows infringed Apple patents was settled,[\[170\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-Microsoft_investment-170) and [Internet Explorer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_Explorer_for_Mac "Internet Explorer for Mac") would ship as the Macintosh's default browser, with the user able to have a preference. Microsoft chairman [Bill Gates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Gates "Bill Gates") appeared on-screen explaining plans for developing Mac software, and expressing excitement to be helping Apple return to success. Jobs addressed the audience:

> If we want to move forward and see Apple healthy and prospering again, we have to let go of a few things here. We have to let go of this notion that for Apple to win, Microsoft has to lose. We have to embrace a notion that for Apple to win, Apple has to do a really good job. And if others are going to help us that's great, because we need all the help we can get, and if we screw up and we don't do a good job, it's not somebody else's fault, it's our fault. So I think that is a very important perspective. If we want Microsoft Office on the Mac, we better treat the company that puts it out with a little bit of gratitude; we'd like their software.
>
> So, the era of setting this up as a competition between Apple and Microsoft is over as far as I'm concerned. This is about getting Apple healthy, this is about Apple being able to make incredibly great contributions to the industry and to get healthy and prosper again.

The day before the announcement Apple had a market cap of $2.46 billion,[\[171\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-171) and had ended its previous quarter with quarterly revenues of US$1.7 billion and cash reserves of US$1.2 billion,[\[172\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-172) making the US$150 million amount of the investment largely symbolic. Apple CFO Fred Anderson stated that Apple would use the additional funds to invest in its core markets of education and creative content.[\[170\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-Microsoft_investment-170)

### iMac, iBook, and Power Mac G4

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/IMac_Bondi_Blue.jpg/500px-IMac_Bondi_Blue.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:IMac_Bondi_Blue.jpg) The original [iMac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMac "IMac") ( [iMac G3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMac_G3 "IMac G3")) released in 1998

While discontinuing Apple's licensing of its operating system to third-party computer manufacturers, one of Jobs's first moves as new acting CEO was to develop the [iMac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMac "IMac"), which bought Apple time to restructure. The original iMac integrated a CRT display and CPU into a streamlined, translucent plastic body. The line became a sales smash, moving about one million units each year. It helped re-introduce Apple to the media and public and announced the company's new emphasis on the design and aesthetics of its products.

In 1999, Apple introduced the [Power Mac G4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_Mac_G4 "Power Mac G4"), which utilized the Motorola-made PowerPC 7400 containing a 128-bit instruction unit known as [AltiVec](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AltiVec "AltiVec"), its flagship processor line. Apple unveiled the [iBook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBook "IBook") that year, its first consumer-oriented laptop, the first Macintosh to support the use of [Wireless LAN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wireless_LAN "Wireless LAN") via the optional AirPort card. Based on the 802.11b standard, it helped popularize Wireless LAN technology to connect computers to networks.

### Mac OS X

Main article: [Mac OS X](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mac_OS_X "Mac OS X")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Apple_Headquarters_in_Cupertino.jpg/500px-Apple_Headquarters_in_Cupertino.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Apple_Headquarters_in_Cupertino.jpg) Company headquarters on Infinite Loop in [Cupertino, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cupertino,_California "Cupertino, California")

In 2001, Apple introduced [Mac OS X](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacOS "MacOS"), an operating system based on [NeXT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NeXT "NeXT")'s [NeXTSTEP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NeXTSTEP "NeXTSTEP") and incorporating parts of the [FreeBSD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FreeBSD "FreeBSD") kernel.[\[173\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-173) Aimed at consumers and professionals alike, Mac OS X married the stability, reliability and security of [Unix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix "Unix") with the ease of a completely overhauled user interface. To help users transition, the new operating system allowed the use of Mac OS 9 applications through the [Classic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classic_(Mac_OS_X) "Classic (Mac OS X)") environment. Apple's [Carbon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_(API) "Carbon (API)") API allowed developers to adapt Mac OS 9 software to use Mac OS X's features.

### Retail stores

Main article: [Apple Store](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Store "Apple Store")

In May 2001, after much speculation, Apple announced the opening of a line of Apple retail stores, to be located throughout the major U.S. computer buying markets. The stores were designed for two primary purposes: to stem the tide of Apple's declining share of the computer market and to respond to poor marketing of Apple products at third-party retail outlets.

## 2001–2007: iPods, iTunes Store, Intel transition

### iPod

Main article: [iPod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod "IPod")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d1/IPod_1G.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:IPod_1G.jpg) A 1st-generation [iPod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod "IPod") (2001)[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8d/IPod_mini.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:IPod_mini.png) [iPod Mini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod_Mini "IPod Mini") with the UI (user interface) set to German

In October 2001, Apple introduced its first [iPod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod "IPod") portable digital audio player. Then iPod started as a 5 gigabyte player capable of storing around 1000 songs. It then evolved into an array of products including the [Mini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod_Mini "IPod Mini") (discontinued), the [iPod Touch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod_Touch "IPod Touch") (discontinued), the [Shuffle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod_Shuffle "IPod Shuffle") (discontinued), the [iPod Classic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod_Classic "IPod Classic") (discontinued), the [Nano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod_Nano "IPod Nano") (discontinued), the [iPhone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone "IPhone") and the [iPad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad "IPad"). Since March 2011, the largest storage capacity for an iPod has been 160 gigabytes.[\[174\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-174) Speaking to software developers on June 6, 2005, Jobs said the company's share of the entire portable music device market stood at 76%.[\[175\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-175)

The iPod gave an enormous lift to Apple's financial results.[\[176\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-176) In the quarter ending March 26, 2005, Apple earned US$290 million, or 34¢ a share, on sales of US$3.24 billion. The year before in the same quarter, Apple earned just US$46 million, or 6¢ a share, on revenue of US$1.91 billion.

### Moving on from colored plastics and the PowerPC G3

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/IMac_G4_sunflower7.png/500px-IMac_G4_sunflower7.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:IMac_G4_sunflower7.png) [iMac G4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMac_G4 "IMac G4") (2002)

In early 2002, Apple unveiled a completely redesigned iMac, using the G4 processor and a [liquid-crystal display](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liquid-crystal_display "Liquid-crystal display"). The new [iMac G4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMac_G4 "IMac G4") design had a white hemispherical base and a flat panel all-digital display supported by a swiveling chrome neck. After several iterations increasing the processing speed and screen sizes from 15" to 17" to 20" the iMac G4 was discontinued and replaced by the [iMac G5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMac_G5 "IMac G5") in the summer of 2004.

Later in 2002, Apple released the [Xserve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xserve "Xserve") [1U](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rack_unit "Rack unit") [rack mounted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rack_mount "Rack mount") server. Originally featuring two G4 chips, the Xserve was unusual for Apple in two ways. It represented an earnest effort to enter the enterprise computer market, and it was cheaper than competitors' similar machines. This was largely due to Fast ATA drives as opposed to the SCSI hard drives used in traditional rack-mounted servers. Apple later released the [Xserve RAID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xserve_RAID "Xserve RAID"), a 14 drive [RAID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RAID "RAID") that was again cheaper than competing systems.

In mid-2003, Jobs launched the [Power Mac G5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_Mac_G5 "Power Mac G5"), based on [IBM](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM "IBM")'s [G5 processor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PowerPC_970 "PowerPC 970"). Its all-metal [anodized aluminum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anodized_aluminum "Anodized aluminum") chassis finished Apple's transition away from colored plastics in their computers. Apple claims this was the first 64-bit computer sold to the general public. The Power Mac G5 was used by Virginia Tech to build its prototype [System X](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_X_(supercomputer) "System X (supercomputer)") supercomputing cluster, which at the time was considered the third-fastest supercomputer in the world. It cost only US$5.2 million to build, far less than the previous No. 3 and other ranking supercomputers. Apple's Xserves were updated to use the G5 as well. They replaced the Power Mac G5 machines as the main building block of [Virginia Tech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virginia_Tech "Virginia Tech")'s [System X](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_X_(supercomputer) "System X (supercomputer)"), which was ranked in November 2004 as the world's seventh-fastest [supercomputer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supercomputer "Supercomputer").[\[177\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-177)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/IMac_G5_-_Frontal_view.png/500px-IMac_G5_-_Frontal_view.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:IMac_G5_-_Frontal_view.png) [iMac G5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMac_G5 "IMac G5") (2004)

A new iMac based on the G5 processor was unveiled August 31, 2004, and was made available in mid-September. This model dispensed with the base altogether, placing the CPU and the rest of the computing hardware behind the flat-panel screen, which is suspended from a streamlined aluminum foot. This new iMac, dubbed the [iMac G5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMac_G5 "IMac G5"), was the "world's thinnest desktop computer",[\[178\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-178) measuring in at around two inches (around 5 centimeters).[\[179\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-179)

In 2004, after creating a sizable financial base to work with, the company began experimenting with new parts from new suppliers. Apple could produce new designs quickly, and released the iPod Video, then the iPod Classic, and eventually the iPod touch and iPhone. On April 29, 2005, Apple released [Mac OS X v10.4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mac_OS_X_v10.4 "Mac OS X v10.4") "Tiger".

Apple's successful [PowerBook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PowerBook "PowerBook") and [iBook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBook "IBook") relied on previous generation G4 architecture produced by [Freescale Semiconductor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freescale_Semiconductor "Freescale Semiconductor"), a spin-off from Motorola. IBM engineers had some success in making their PowerPC G5 processor consume less power and run cooler, but not enough to run in iBook or PowerBook formats. In October 2005, Apple released the Power Mac G5 Dual featuring a Dual-Core processor – two cores in one rather than two separate processors. The Power Mac G5 Quad uses two Dual-Core processors. The Power Mac G5 Dual cores run individually at 2.0GHz or 2.3GHz. The Power Mac G5 Quad cores run individually at 2.5GHz, and all variations have a graphics processor with 256-bit memory bandwidth.[\[180\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-180)

### Retail store expansion

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Apple_Store_Ginza_%282006.05%29.jpg/500px-Apple_Store_Ginza_%282006.05%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Apple_Store_Ginza_(2006.05).jpg) Apple Store in Ginza district, [Tokyo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tokyo "Tokyo")

Initially, [Apple Stores](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Store "Apple Store") were only in the United States, but in late 2003, Apple opened its first Apple Store abroad, in Tokyo's [Ginza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ginza "Ginza") district. It was followed by a store in [Osaka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osaka,_Osaka "Osaka, Osaka"), Japan in August 2004. In 2005, Apple opened stores in [Nagoya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nagoya,_Aichi "Nagoya, Aichi"), the [Shibuya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shibuya,_Tokyo "Shibuya, Tokyo") district of Tokyo, [Fukuoka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fukuoka,_Fukuoka "Fukuoka, Fukuoka"), and [Sendai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sendai,_Miyagi "Sendai, Miyagi"). A store opened in [Sapporo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sapporo,_Hokkaid%C5%8D "Sapporo, Hokkaidō") in 2006. Apple's first European store opened in London, on [Regent Street](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regent_Street "Regent Street"), in November 2004. A store in the [Bullring](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bull_Ring,_Birmingham "Bull Ring, Birmingham") shopping centre in [Birmingham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birmingham "Birmingham") opened in April 2005, and the [Bluewater shopping centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bluewater_Shopping_Centre "Bluewater Shopping Centre") in [Dartford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dartford "Dartford"), Kent opened in July 2005. Apple opened its first store in Canada in the middle of 2005 at the [Yorkdale Shopping Centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yorkdale_Shopping_Centre "Yorkdale Shopping Centre") in [North York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_York "North York"), [Toronto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toronto "Toronto"). Later in 2005 Apple opened the [Meadowhall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meadowhall_Centre "Meadowhall Centre") Store in [Sheffield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheffield "Sheffield") and the [Trafford Centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trafford_Centre "Trafford Centre") Store in [Manchester](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchester "Manchester"), UK. Later additions in the London area include [Brent Cross](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brent_Cross "Brent Cross") (January 2006), [Westfield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Westfield_London "Westfield London") in Shepherd's Bush (September 2008), and [Covent Garden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Covent_Garden "Covent Garden") (August 2010), which at 40,000 square feet (3,700m2) was, as of 2015[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Apple_Inc.&action=edit), the largest Apple Store in the world.[\[181\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-181)

Apple opened several "larger" stores in October 2004 to capture markets where demand does not necessarily dictate a full-scale store. The first of these stores was opened at [Stanford Shopping Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_Shopping_Center "Stanford Shopping Center") in [Palo Alto, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California "Palo Alto, California"). These stores are only one half the square footage of the smallest normal store.

### Apple and "i" Web services

In 2000, Apple introduced iTools, a set of free web-based tools that included an email account, internet greeting cards called iCards, a Web site review service called [iReview](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IReview "IReview"), and "KidSafe", to prevent children browsing inappropriate websites. The latter two services were canceled because of lack of success. iCards and email were integrated into Apple's [.Mac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/.Mac ".Mac") subscription-based service introduced in 2002 and discontinued in mid-2008 to make way for MobileMe, coinciding with the iPhone 3G release. MobileMe, at the same US$99.00 annual subscription as its dotMac predecessor, featured "push" services to instantly and automatically send emails, contacts and calendar updates directly to users' iPhones. Controversy around the release of MobileMe resulted in downtime and a significantly longer release window. Apple extended existing MobileMe subscriptions by 30 days free-of-charge.[\[182\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-182) At the WWDC event in June 2011, Apple announced [iCloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ICloud "ICloud"), keeping most MobileMe services but dropping iDisk, Gallery, and iWeb. It added Find my Mac, iTunes Match, Photo Stream, Documents & Data Backup, and iCloud backup for iOS devices. The service requires iOS 5 and OS X 10.7 Lion.

### iTunes Store

Main article: [iTunes Store](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ITunes_Store "ITunes Store")

The [iTunes Music Store](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ITunes_Store "ITunes Store") was launched in April 2003, with 2 million downloads in the first 16 days. Music was purchased through the [iTunes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ITunes "ITunes") application, which was initially Macintosh-only; in October 2003, support for [Windows](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Windows "Microsoft Windows") was added. Initially, the music store was only available in the United States due to licensing restrictions.

In June 2004 Apple opened its iTunes Music Store in the United Kingdom, France, and Germany. A version for the [European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union") version opened October 2004, but it was not initially available in the [Republic of Ireland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland "Republic of Ireland") due to the intransigence of the [Irish Recorded Music Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irish_Recorded_Music_Association "Irish Recorded Music Association") (IRMA) but was opened there a few months later on Thursday, January 6, 2005. A version for Canada opened in December 2004. On May 10, 2005, the iTunes Music Store was expanded to [Denmark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denmark "Denmark"), Norway, [Sweden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweden "Sweden"), and [Switzerland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Switzerland "Switzerland").

On December 16, 2004, Apple sold its 200 millionth song on the iTunes Music Store to Ryan Alekman from [Belchertown, Massachusetts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belchertown,_Massachusetts "Belchertown, Massachusetts"). The download was _[The Complete U2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Complete_U2 "The Complete U2")_, by [U2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U2 "U2").[\[183\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-183) Just under three months later Apple sold its 300 millionth song on March 2, 2005.[\[184\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-184) On July 17, 2005, the iTunes Music Store sold its 500 millionth song.[\[185\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-185) At that point, songs were selling at an accelerating annualized rate of more than 500 million.

On October 25, 2005, the iTunes Store went live in Australia, with songs selling for [A$](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australian_dollar "Australian dollar") 1.69 each, albums at (generally) A$16.99 and music videos and Pixar short films at A$3.39. Before the loophole was closed, people in [New Zealand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand "New Zealand") were briefly able to buy music from the Australian store On February 23, 2006, the iTunes Music Store sold its 1 billionth song.[\[186\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-186)

The iTunes Music Store changed its name to iTunes Store on September 12, 2006, when it began offering video content (TV shows and movies) for sale. Since iTunes' inception, it has sold over 2 billion songs, 1.2 billion of which were sold in 2006. Since downloadable TV and movie content was added 50 million TV episodes and 1.3 million movies have been downloaded. In early 2010, Apple celebrated the 10 billionth song downloaded from the iTunes Music Store.[\[187\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-187)

### Intel transition

Main article: [Mac transition to Intel processors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mac_transition_to_Intel_processors "Mac transition to Intel processors")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/MacBook_Pro.png/500px-MacBook_Pro.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:MacBook_Pro.png) [MacBook Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacBook_Pro "MacBook Pro") Intel-based (2006)

In a keynote address on June 6, 2005, Jobs announced that Apple would produce Intel-based Macintosh computers beginning in 2006.[\[188\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-188) Jobs confirmed rumors that the company had been secretly producing versions of [Mac OS X](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacOS "MacOS") for both PowerPC and Intel processors over the past 5 years, and that the transition to Intel processor systems would last until the end of 2007. Rumors of cross-platform compatibility had been spurred by the fact that Mac OS X is based on [OPENSTEP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OPENSTEP "OPENSTEP"), an operating system that was available for many platforms. Apple's own [Darwin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darwin_(operating_system) "Darwin (operating system)"), the [open source](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open-source_software "Open-source software") underpinnings of Mac OS X, was also available for Intel's x86 architecture.[\[189\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-189)[\[190\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-190)[\[191\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-191)

On January 10, 2006, the Intel-based [iMac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMac "IMac") and [MacBook Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacBook_Pro "MacBook Pro") were introduced,[\[192\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-192)[\[193\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-193) based on the [Intel Core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intel_Core "Intel Core") Duo platform. They came alongside news that Apple would complete the transition to Intel processors on all hardware by the end of 2006, a year ahead of the originally quoted schedule.

## 2007–2011: Apple Inc., iPhone, iOS, iPad

On January 9, 2007, Apple Computer, Inc. shortened its name to simply Apple Inc. In his [Macworld Expo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macworld_Expo "Macworld Expo") keynote address, Jobs explained that with their current product mix consisting of the iPod and Apple TV as well as their Macintosh brand, Apple really wasn't just a computer company anymore. At the same address, Jobs revealed a product that would revolutionize an industry in which Apple had never previously competed: the Apple [iPhone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone "IPhone"). The iPhone combined Apple's first widescreen iPod with the world's first mobile device boasting visual voicemail, and an internet communicator able to run a fully-functional version of Apple's web browser, [Safari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safari_(web_browser) "Safari (web browser)"), on the then-named [iPhone OS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IOS_version_history#Releases "IOS version history") (later renamed [iOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IOS "IOS")).

### iOS evolution: iPhone and iPad

Main articles: [iOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IOS "IOS"), [iPhone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone "IPhone"), and [iPad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad "IPad")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/IPhone_First_Generation.jpg/500px-IPhone_First_Generation.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:IPhone_First_Generation.jpg) The original [iPhone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_(1st_generation) "IPhone (1st generation)") (2007)

The first version of the iPhone became publicly available on June 29, 2007, in selected countries/markets. It was another 12 months before the [iPhone 3G](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_3G "IPhone 3G") became available on July 11, 2008. Apple announced the [iPhone 3GS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_3GS "IPhone 3GS") on June 8, 2009, along with plans to release it later in June, July, and August, starting with the U.S., Canada, and major European countries on June 19. This 12-month iteration cycle has continued with the [iPhone 4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_4 "IPhone 4") model arriving in similar fashion in 2010, a Verizon model was released in February 2011, and a Sprint model in October 2011, shortly after Jobs' death.

On February 10, 2011, the iPhone 4 was made available on both Verizon Wireless and AT&T. Now two iPod types are multi-touch: the iPod nano and the iPod touch, a big advance in technology. Apple TV currently has a 2nd-generation model, which is 4 times smaller than the original Apple TV. Apple has also gone wireless, selling a wireless trackpad, keyboard, mouse, and external hard drive. Wired accessories are still available.

The Apple [iPad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad "IPad") was announced on January 27, 2010, with retail availability commencing in April and systematically growing in markets throughout 2010. The iPad fits into Apple's iOS product line, being twice the screen size of an iPhone without the phone abilities. While there were initial fears of product cannibalization the FY2010 financial results released in Jan 2011 included commentary of a reverse 'halo' effect, where iPad sales were leading to increased sales of iMacs and MacBooks.[\[194\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-194)

### Resurgence compared to Microsoft

Since 2005, Apple's revenues, profits, and stock price have grown significantly. On May 26, 2010, Apple's stock market value overtook Microsoft's,[\[195\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-195)[\[196\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-196)[\[197\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-197) and Apple's revenues surpassed those of Microsoft in the third quarter of 2010.[\[198\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-198)[\[199\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-199) After giving their results for the first quarter of 2011, Microsoft's net profits of $5.2 billion were lower for the quarter than those of Apple, which earned $6 billion in net profit for the quarter.[\[200\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-Apple_Microsoft_revenue-200)[\[201\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-201) The late April announcement of profits by the companies marked the first time in 20 years that Microsoft's profits had been lower than Apple's,[\[202\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-Apple_Microsoft_20_years-202) a situation described by _[Ars Technica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ars_Technica "Ars Technica")_ as "unimaginable a decade ago".[\[200\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-Apple_Microsoft_revenue-200)

_[The Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian "The Guardian")_ reported that one of the reasons for the change was because PC software, where Microsoft dominates, has become less important compared to the tablet and smartphone markets, where Apple has a strong presence.[\[202\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-Apple_Microsoft_20_years-202) One reason for this was a surprise drop in PC sales in the quarter.[\[202\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-Apple_Microsoft_20_years-202) Another issue for Microsoft was that its online search business had lost a lot of money, with a loss of $700 million in the first quarter of 2010.[\[202\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-Apple_Microsoft_20_years-202)

## 2011–2020: Restructuring and Apple Watch

See also: [Apple car project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_car_project "Apple car project")

On March 2, 2011, Apple unveiled the iPad's second-generation model, the [iPad 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_2 "IPad 2"). Like the 4th-generation iPod Touch and iPhone, the iPad 2 comes with a front-facing camera as well as a rear-facing camera, along with three new apps that utilize these new features: Camera, [FaceTime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FaceTime "FaceTime"), and [Photo Booth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photo_Booth "Photo Booth"). On August 24, Jobs resigned from his position as CEO,[\[203\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-203) with Tim Cook taking his place.

On October 29, 2012, Apple announced structural changes to increase collaboration between hardware, software, and services.[\[204\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-204) This involved the departure of [Scott Forstall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scott_Forstall "Scott Forstall"), responsible for the launch of iOS (iPhone OS at the time of launch), who was replaced with [Craig Federighi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Craig_Federighi "Craig Federighi") as head of iOS and OS X teams. [Jony Ive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jony_Ive "Jony Ive") became head of HI (Human Interface), whilst [Eddy Cue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eddy_Cue "Eddy Cue") was announced as head of online services including Siri and Maps. The most notable short term difference of this restructuring was the launch of [iOS 7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IOS_7 "IOS 7"), the first version of the operating system to use a drastically different design to its predecessors, headed by Jony Ive,[\[205\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-205) followed by [OS X Yosemite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OS_X_Yosemite "OS X Yosemite") a year later with a similar design.

During this time, Apple released the [iPhone 5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_5 "IPhone 5"), the first iPhone to have a screen larger than 3.5",[\[206\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-206) the [iPod Touch 5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod_Touch_5 "IPod Touch 5") with a 4" screen, the [iPhone 5S](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_5S "IPhone 5S") with fingerprint scanning technology in the form of [Touch ID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Touch_ID "Touch ID"), and [iPhone 6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_6 "IPhone 6") and [iPhone 6 Plus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_6_Plus "IPhone 6 Plus"), with screens at 4.7" and 5.5". They released the [3rd-generation iPad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_(3rd_generation) "IPad (3rd generation)") with Retina Display, followed by the [4th-generation iPad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_(4th_generation) "IPad (4th generation)") just half a year later. The [iPad Mini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_Mini "IPad Mini") was announced alongside the iPad 4th gen, and was the first to feature a smaller screen than 9.7". This was followed by the [iPad Mini 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_Mini_2 "IPad Mini 2") with Retina Display in 2013, alongside the [iPad Air](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_Air "IPad Air"), a continuation of the original 9.7" range of iPads, which was subsequently followed by the [iPad Air 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_Air_2 "IPad Air 2") with Touch ID in 2014. Apple released various major Mac updates, including the [MacBook Pro with Retina Display](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacBook_Pro_with_Retina_Display "MacBook Pro with Retina Display"),[\[207\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-207) whilst discontinuing the original [MacBook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacBook "MacBook") range for a short period, before reintroducing it in 2015 with various new features, a Retina Display and a new design that implemented [USB-C](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USB-C "USB-C"), while removing all other ports.[\[208\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-208) The [Mac Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mac_Pro "Mac Pro") and [iMac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMac "IMac") were updated with more power and a drastically smaller and thinner profile. On November 25, 2013, Apple acquired a company called PrimeSense.[\[209\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-209)

On May 28, 2014, Apple acquired [Beats Electronics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beats_Electronics "Beats Electronics"), producers of the popular [Beats by Dre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beats_by_Dre "Beats by Dre") headphone and speaker range, as well as streaming service [Beats Music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beats_Music "Beats Music"). On September 9, 2014, Apple announced the [Apple Watch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Watch "Apple Watch"), the first new product range since the departure of Jobs.[\[210\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-210) The product cannot function beyond basic features without being within Bluetooth or WiFi range to an iPhone and contains basic applications (many acting as a remote for other devices, such as a music remote, or a control for an Apple TV) and fitness tracking. The Apple Watch received mixed reviews, with critics suggesting that whilst the device showed promise, it lacked a clear purpose, similar to many of the devices already on the market.[\[211\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-211) The Apple Watch was released on April 24, 2015.[\[212\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-212)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Apple_Watch_Demo.jpg/500px-Apple_Watch_Demo.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Apple_Watch_Demo.jpg) [Apple Watch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Watch "Apple Watch") first generation (2015)

On September 9, 2015, Apple announced the [iPhone 6S](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_6S "IPhone 6S") and [iPhone 6S Plus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_6S_Plus "IPhone 6S Plus") with 3D Touch, the [iPad Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_Pro "IPad Pro"), and the fourth-generation [Apple TV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_TV_(device) "Apple TV (device)"), along with the fourth-generation [iPad Mini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_Mini "IPad Mini").
On March 21, 2016, Apple announced the [first-generation iPhone SE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_SE_(1st_generation) "IPhone SE (1st generation)") and the smaller [iPad Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_Pro "IPad Pro").

On September 7, 2016, Apple announced the [iPhone 7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_7 "IPhone 7") and [iPhone 7 Plus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_7_Plus "IPhone 7 Plus") with an improved camera and a faster processor than the previous generation. The iPhone 7 and iPhone 7 Plus have high storage options.
On October 27, 2016, Apple announced the new 13 and 15 inch [MacBook Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacBook_Pro "MacBook Pro") with a retina Touch Bar.
On March 21, 2017, Apple announced the [iPad (2017)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_(2017) "IPad (2017)"). This is the iPad Air 2 successor, equipped with a faster processor, and starts at $329. Apple also announced the (Product)RED iPhone 7 and iPhone 7 Plus.

On June 5, 2017, Apple announced [iOS 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IOS_11 "IOS 11") as well as new versions of [macOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacOS "MacOS"), [watchOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WatchOS "WatchOS"), and [tvOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TvOS "TvOS"). Updated versions of the iMac, MacBook Pro, and MacBook were released, along with the 10.5 and 12.9 inch [iPad Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPad_Pro "IPad Pro"), and " [HomePod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HomePod "HomePod")", a Siri speaker similar to the [Amazon Echo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_Echo "Amazon Echo"). On September 12, at the [Steve Jobs Theater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Jobs_Theater "Steve Jobs Theater"), Apple introduced the [iPhone 8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_8 "IPhone 8") and iPhone 8 Plus with better camera features, more improvements in [product design](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Product_design "Product design"), [user experience](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_experience "User experience"), performance and more, and announced the [iPhone X](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_X "IPhone X") with facial recognition technology and wireless charging. Apple announced the 4K Apple TV with 4K, HDR and Dolby Vision experience, and the Apple Watch Series 3, supporting a cellular connection, running [watchOS 4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WatchOS "WatchOS").

In March 2018, [_Bloomberg_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bloomberg_News "Bloomberg News") reported that Apple was developing [MicroLED](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MicroLED "MicroLED") screens for the iPhone, iPad, Mac, watch, AR glasses, and [electric car](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_car_project "Apple car project").[\[213\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-213)[\[214\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-214)[\[215\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-215) It was linked to a Research and Development facility in [Santa Clara, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santa_Clara,_California "Santa Clara, California") code named Aria[\[216\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-216) by the _Bay Area News Group_.[\[217\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-217) On September 12, at the [Steve Jobs Theater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Jobs_Theater "Steve Jobs Theater"), Apple introduced the [iPhone XS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_XS "IPhone XS"), [iPhone XS Max](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_XS "IPhone XS"), and [iPhone XR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_XR "IPhone XR"), running [iOS 12](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IOS_12 "IOS 12"), with improved facial recognition and HDR in the display as well as better cameras for all 3 phones. They also announced the Apple Watch Series 4, running [watchOS 5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WatchOS "WatchOS"), with an all-new design and larger display as well as many more health-related features.

In October 2018, _Bloomberg_ reported that, as early as 2015, a specialized unit of China's [People's Liberation Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People's_Liberation_Army "People's Liberation Army") began inserting chips into [Supermicro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermicro "Supermicro") servers that allowed for [backdoor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backdoor_(computing) "Backdoor (computing)") access to them.[\[218\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-BB-218) Approximately 30 companies reportedly had their servers compromised via the chips, including Apple Inc.[\[218\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-BB-218) On September 20, 2019, the [iPhone 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_11 "IPhone 11"), [iPhone 11 Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_11_Pro "IPhone 11 Pro"), and iPhone 11 Pro Max were introduced. The iPhone 11 Pro was the first iPhone to feature three cameras.

## 2020–present: 5G and Apple silicon

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Macbook_Air_M1_Silver_PNG.png/500px-Macbook_Air_M1_Silver_PNG.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Macbook_Air_M1_Silver_PNG.png) [MacBook Air M1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacBook_Air_(Apple_silicon) "MacBook Air (Apple silicon)") (2020)

In 2020, Apple was fined £21 million euros, claiming they intentionally slowed down older models of iPhones to [encourage people to buy newer models](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planned_obsolescence "Planned obsolescence"). The company somewhat admitted to this practice in 2017, saying the phones were slowed to respond to the [decay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capacity_loss "Capacity loss") of iPhones' [lithium-ion batteries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery "Lithium-ion battery"), which made it harder for the batteries to reach the phones' expected power demands.[\[219\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-219) The [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic "COVID-19 pandemic") heavily affected China, hurting Apple financially, because they invested into China enough to become increasingly dependent on the country.[\[220\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-O'Flaherty-220) Chinese factories closed and demand for Apple products went down.[\[221\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-221) However, they recovered and eventually reached a US$2 trillion market cap later that year.[\[222\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-222) The [iPhone 12](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_12 "IPhone 12"), [12 Pro, and 12 Pro Max](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_12_Pro "IPhone 12 Pro") were introduced, being the first iPhones to support [5G](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/5G "5G") connectivity.[\[223\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-223) The company also started using its own [Apple silicon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_silicon "Apple silicon") processors in Macs, instead of chips made by Intel.[\[224\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-224)[\[225\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-225)

In April 2021, the M1-powered iPad was launched, along with a new M1-powered iMac offered in 7 colors, recalling the [iMacs offered in 5 colors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMac_G3#Model_line-up "IMac G3") announced in 1999. Apple launched a GPS tracking device called [AirTag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AirTag "AirTag") that uses the Apple's [Find My](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Find_My "Find My") device network. In 2021 and 2022, Apple repeated its pattern of introducing four new iPhones in September, with 2021's [iPhone 13](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_13 "IPhone 13") and [iPhone 13 Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_13_Pro "IPhone 13 Pro") lines and 2022's [iPhone 14](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_14 "IPhone 14") and [iPhone 14 Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_14_Pro "IPhone 14 Pro") lines. The iPhone 14 Pro ditched the [notch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Notch_(engineering) "Notch (engineering)") containing the sensors for a "dynamic island", which allows for space between the top edge of the screen and the sensors for Face ID. 2022 saw Apple announce the first Macs with Apple's [M2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_M2 "Apple M2") chip and a new sub-series of Apple Watch with increased performance for outdoor activities named [Apple Watch Ultra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Watch_Ultra "Apple Watch Ultra").

Apple experienced a period of unprecedented employee unrest in 2021 and 2022, resulting in outspoken employees organizing over labor issues and the company's treatment of women at the company in its corporate offices and retail stores.[\[226\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-:3-226)[\[227\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-227) Employees engaged in [hashtag activism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hashtag_activism "Hashtag activism") on social media inspired by the [#MeToo movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MeToo_movement "MeToo movement") called [#AppleToo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AppleToo "AppleToo")[\[228\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-228) and two American stores [unionized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Inc._and_unions "Apple Inc. and unions") for the first time.[\[229\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-229)

In 2022, Apple paused all product sales in Russia in response to the country's [invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Russian invasion of Ukraine").[\[230\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-230) Tim Cook began focusing on privacy features, which lowered App Store developers' revenue. They also developed App Tracking Transparency, a set of privacy features which cost Facebook US$12 billion.[\[220\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-O'Flaherty-220) The company also announced they would start including ads in the Books, Maps, and TV iOS apps,[\[231\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-231) and that it would eventually move production out of China.[\[232\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-232)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Apple_Vision_Pro_on_display.jpg/500px-Apple_Vision_Pro_on_display.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Apple_Vision_Pro_on_display.jpg) An [Apple Vision Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Vision_Pro "Apple Vision Pro") headset on display

Apple launched a [buy now, pay later](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buy_now,_pay_later "Buy now, pay later") service called 'Apple Pay Later' for its [Apple Wallet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Wallet "Apple Wallet") users in 2023. The program allows its users to apply for loans between $50 and $1,000 to make online or in-app purchases, and then repaying them through four installments spread over six weeks without any interest or fees.[\[233\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-233)[\[234\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-234) In June, Apple released the [Apple Vision Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Vision_Pro "Apple Vision Pro"), a computer in the form of an [augmented reality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augmented_reality "Augmented reality") headset which runs the [visionOS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VisionOS "VisionOS") operating system. Wearers of the headset use hand gestures to navigate the user interface.[\[235\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-235) It initially released at $3,500 in the United States, and while sales figures have not been released as of June2024[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=History_of_Apple_Inc.&action=edit), it is considered to be a financial failure in its initial stages.[\[236\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-236) The company then reached a $25 million settlement in a [U.S. Department of Justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice "United States Department of Justice") case that alleged they were discriminating against U.S. citizens in hiring; they created jobs that were not listed online and required paper submission to apply for, while advertising these jobs to foreign workers as part of recruitment for [PERM](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_Labor_Certification#Program_electronic_review_management "Permanent Labor Certification").[\[237\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-237)

In April 2024, Apple laid off more than 600 employees working in facilities linked to the electric car project and microLED development.[\[238\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-238) The projects had been reported to have been shut down in the preceding two months.[\[239\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-239)[\[240\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-240)

In June 2024, Apple announced [iOS18](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IOS_18 "IOS 18") and [macOS Sequoia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MacOS_Sequoia "MacOS Sequoia") in their [WWDC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Worldwide_Developers_Conference "Worldwide Developers Conference") 2024 event.[\[241\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-241)[\[242\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-242) After the development of powerful [AI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") software like [OpenAI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OpenAI "OpenAI")'s [ChatGPT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ChatGPT "ChatGPT") in the early 2020s, Apple was accused of being behind their competitors in innovating using AI;[\[243\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-243) alongside the new operating systems, the company announced they would introduce AI features into their products, such as using ChatGPT to improve Siri. The first product to feature these improvements, named [Apple Intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Intelligence "Apple Intelligence"), is planned to be the [iPhone 15 Pro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone_15_Pro "IPhone 15 Pro") running [iOS 18](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IOS_18 "IOS 18").[\[244\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-244) Criticism was leveled towards the plan to incorporate recorded user inputs into ChatGPT's [data set](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_set "Data set").[\[245\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-245) Apple did not pay OpenAI for these features, believing that exposure to OpenAI products will already financially benefit them.[\[246\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-246) The announcement improved Apple's stock, temporarily making them the world's most valuable company instead of Microsoft.[\[247\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-247)

In 2024, Apple was sued by two female employees seeking class action who claimed that the company's hiring and performance-review practices are biased against women.[\[248\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-248) Meanwhile, the [National Labor Relations Board](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Labor_Relations_Board "National Labor Relations Board") (NLRB) charged Apple with violations of the [National Labor Relations Act of 1935](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Labor_Relations_Act_of_1935 "National Labor Relations Act of 1935") in spring and fall of 2024. The NLRB accused Apple of maintaining unlawful employee contracts, rules around social media and [Slack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slack_(software) "Slack (software)") usage, for interrogating unionizing employees, and for illegally firing [Janneke Parrish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Janneke_Parrish "Janneke Parrish"), a labor activist who had co-lead the #AppleToo movement.[\[249\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-249)[\[250\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-250)[\[251\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-251)

## Financial history

As cash reserves increased significantly in 2006, Apple created [Braeburn Capital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braeburn_Capital "Braeburn Capital") on April 6, 2006, to manage its assets.[\[252\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-252)

| FY 1985 | 1,918 | 61 | 27% | 3% |

| FY 1990 | 5,558 | 475 | 5% | 9% |

### Stock

'AAPL' is the [stock symbol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stock_symbol "Stock symbol") under which [Apple Inc.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Inc. "Apple Inc.") trades on the [NASDAQ](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASDAQ "NASDAQ") [stock market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stock_market "Stock market"). Apple originally went public on December 12, 1980, with an [initial public offering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Initial_public_offering "Initial public offering") at US$22.00[\[256\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-256) per share. The stock has split 2 for 1 three times on June 15, 1987, June 21, 2000, and February 28, 2005. Apple initially paid dividends from June 15, 1987, to December 15, 1995. On March 19, 2012, Apple announced that it would again start paying a dividend of $2.65 per quarter (beginning in the quarter that starts in July 2012) along a $10 billion [share buyback](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Share_repurchase "Share repurchase") that would commence September 30, 2012, the start of its fiscal 2013 year. Gene Munster and Michael Olson of [Piper Jaffray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Piper_Jaffray "Piper Jaffray") are the main analysts who track Apple stock. Piper Jaffray estimates future stock and revenue of Apple annually, and have been doing so for several years.[\[257\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Apple_Inc.#cite_note-257)

Title: History of Apple: Company timeline and facts - TheStreet
[Skip to main content](https://www.thestreet.com/technology/history-of-apple-company-timeline-facts#main-content)

# History of Apple: Company timeline and facts

The two Steves started Apple in a garage in the 1970s. Today, the maker of MacBooks, iPhones, and AirPods is valued at nearly $4 trillion. Here’s how it happened.

Jan 8, 2026 12:02 AM EST

![](https://www.thestreet.com/.image/MTk4NjQyNTYxMTczMTY5OTI3/0.jpg?io=1&profile=w256&ar=1-1)

By [Dominic Diongson](https://www.thestreet.com/author/dominic-diongson)

Reviewed by [Jeremy Salvucci](https://www.thestreet.com/author/jeremysalvucci)

0

[Add us on](https://www.google.com/preferences/source?q=thestreet.com)

![Steve Jobs, chief executive officer of Apple Inc., right, speaks in front of a file photograph of himself and Apple co-founder Steve Wozniak during the launch of the Apple iPad tablet at the Yerba Buena Center for the Arts Theater in San Francisco, California, U.S., on Wednesday, Jan. 27, 2010. Jobs, who built the world's most valuable technology company by creating devices that changed how people use electronics and revolutionized the computer, music and mobile-phone industries, died Wednesday, Oct. 5, 2011. He was 56. Photographer: Tony Avelar/Bloomberg via Getty Images](https://www.thestreet.com/.image/NDA6MDAwMDAwMDAyNzU2MDcx/file-steve-jobs-chief-executive-officer-of-apple-inc-right-speaks-in-front-of-a-file-photograph-of-himself-and-apple-co-founder-steve-wozniak-during-the-launch-of-the-apple-ipad-tablet-at-the-2756071.jpg?io=1&profile=w2560&ar=4-3&x=60&y=31)Steve Jobs and Steve Wozniak built Apple's first computers in Jobs' parents' garage.
